  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer16891308521661775229">Suze is a mediator -- a liaison between the living and the dead. In other words, she sees dead people. And they won't leave her alone until she helps them resolve their unfinished business with the living. But Jesse, the hot ghost haunting her bedroom, doesn't seem to need her help. Which is a relief, because Suze has just moved to sunny California and plans to start fresh</span>
  <span id="freeText16891308521661775229" style="display:none">Suze is a mediator -- a liaison between the living and the dead. In other words, she sees dead people. And they won't leave her alone until she helps them resolve their unfinished business with the living. But Jesse, the hot ghost haunting her bedroom, doesn't seem to need her help. Which is a relief, because Suze has just moved to sunny California and plans to start fresh, with trips to the mall instead of the cemetery, and surfing instead of spectral visitations. But the very first day at her new school, Suze realizes it's not that easy. There's a ghost with revenge on her mind ... and Suze happens to be in the way.</span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/45104691-alisha"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1454018506i/45104691._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/45104691-alisha">Alisha</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't know if you can read it on goodreads but maybe as a pdf on the internet or you could buy the book or borrow from the/a library if you have one<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't know if you can read it on goodreads but maybe as a pdf on the internet or you could buy the book or borrow from the/a library if you have one. EDIT: Wait no, you can go on the arrow at the top menu bar where it says like home / my books / friends etc at the end click on the arrow and then click on Ebooks which is right above "fun" and you could search books and if they have the book you want you click on it and it will give you the option to download it as a pdf. So basically you can read it online. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330785018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5900251452266270734"><br/><b>4.5 stars.</b> Now I remember why Meg Cabot used to be my most favourite author when I was younger. I <em>adored</em> her. This doesn’t mean that I liked every single book she wrote, but I loved the fact that I could just chose the genre I wanted to read with her, know what I’m saying? Contemporary, urban fantasy, paranormal, supernatural, historical… <strong>She’s a versatile writer</strong> <strong>and those types of writers always impress me.</strong><br/><br/>I know why I never read this series. I also know that I acted foolishly by not giving it </span>
  <span id="freeText5900251452266270734" style="display:none"><br /><b>4.5 stars.</b> Now I remember why Meg Cabot used to be my most favourite author when I was younger. I <em>adored</em> her. This doesn’t mean that I liked every single book she wrote, but I loved the fact that I could just chose the genre I wanted to read with her, know what I’m saying? Contemporary, urban fantasy, paranormal, supernatural, historical… <strong>She’s a versatile writer</strong> <strong>and those types of writers always impress me.</strong><br /><br />I know why I never read this series. I also know that I acted foolishly by not giving it a shot. I remember borrowing a couple of The Princess Diaries books from my library and seeing this series next to it. I just never paid much attention to it, because my eleven-year-old self thought it looked… <strong>weird</strong>. That’s right. (I also didn’t like the cover; its colors: lurid, lurid, lurid!) Anyway, it just didn’t look serious enough for me, and when the subject is ghost-related, I like it mature and complex. I know… what was I thinking judging so easily? I guess sometimes it’s actually good to be wrong about books.<br /><br /><strong>This book… This book… It’s near PERFECT.</strong> And it’s so much fun, without there being excessive humour and entertaining but pointless scenes to the plot. The main character is slightly snarky, highly witty, smart and <em>good at what she does</em>. She’s a mediator, and she does her job well. She has experience in talking to ghosts, and it shows. Doesn’t mean it always works out well for her, but she’s always ready to find solutions to problems and protect the people she loves. I didn’t think she and I would get along that much, because sometimes she can be quite rude, and I don’t especially like rude people, but her remarks don’t just come out of nowhere, for no reason; she knows how to defend herself.<br /><br />There’s a bunch of secondary characters to meet and love. Really, there’s not one I managed to hate, even the vile ones. There are stereotypes (even the ghost’s reason for dying wasn’t new to my ear – déja vu, déjà vu, déjà vu) but they won’t bother you because 1) they’re not highlighted and 2) you’ll be so immersed in Suze’s (main character) thoughts that, if <em>she’s</em> not thinking about that, you won’t either. I think maybe I missed Meg Cabot’s stories too much, because I honestly can’t find anything negative that bothered me to say about this. Either that or it’s just that exceptionally entrancing. I guess the romance isn’t that fabulous… but, really, Suze isn’t preoccupied by boys! She has ghosts to deal with, for God’s sake! Well… *wink*<br /><br />Also, it’s fast-paced and I might even have read it in one sitting if I were the type to do that. Realistic and believable, too, otherwise I swear I wouldn’t have liked this. Ghosts are an interesting and important subject to me, so if it’s not well dealt with or if they’re ridiculously portrayed, I get cranky. Why this book doesn’t contain your usual teen-who-sees-ghosts story is because Meg Cabot takes it to a <strong>whole new level</strong>. But I’ll let you discover what the hell I’m talking about.<br /><br /><strong>I can’t even think of one reason why you shouldn’t pick this book up. Extremely recommended to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/237195.Linda_Joy_Singleton" title="Linda Joy Singleton" rel="nofollow noopener">Linda Joy Singleton</a>... and everyone else!</strong><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5900251452266270734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      Young me, of course :P
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689321957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4595965254198094830"><br/><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>But even on the ninth floor of Bellevue-which is where they lock up the crazy people in New York-I probably wouldn't be safe from the ghosts. They'd find me. <br/>They always do.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Alright so, it appears that everyone wanted to like my pre-review of fangirlish relations to when I was younger...so I don't see a large point in writing a long-winded review when it seems everyone has mostly stopped by and saw all they wanted to see. But, along with those youngish nostalgic ramblings, I did want </span>
  <span id="freeText4595965254198094830" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>But even on the ninth floor of Bellevue-which is where they lock up the crazy people in New York-I probably wouldn't be safe from the ghosts. They'd find me. <br>They always do.</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Alright so, it appears that everyone wanted to like my pre-review of fangirlish relations to when I was younger...so I don't see a large point in writing a long-winded review when it seems everyone has mostly stopped by and saw all they wanted to see. But, along with those youngish nostalgic ramblings, I did want to say <i>why</i> I loved-and <i>still</i> love-this series.<br><br>It's not often a person can look back at a book they read in <b>middle school</b> and say they still love it and it's almost just as good as they remember. Maybe it is, maybe it isn't. <b>Maybe I love it so much I'm blind</b> to the fact that it is a little youngish. Maybe it really is just as good as I think it is. Maybe I am biased because I truly believe this author is a witty, sarcastic, and wonderful writer. Or maybe I'm just biased for Jesse. And Suze. <u>I don't know</u>, and frankly, <b>who the fuck cares?</b> <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Oh, Suze. Not again."</blockquote>
</b><br><br>This series shaped a large chunk of my pre-teen years and gave me countless months, years, whatever of pining and wanting and dreaming of the beautiful Jesse. And, admittedly, my funny story for this is that I read book five first. ME. CHELSEA. The girl who hates spoilers and disorder and messing with the integrity of books. But I guess this just goes to show you that if you are a good author, you can make anything work.<br><br>I was OBSESSED with that fifth book, Haunted, and wanted nothing more than for Jesse and Suze's story to continue. Little did I know, after a little bout of research at the local bookstore (aahhh the good old brick and mortar days) that I had missed four books before!! Imagine how <i>excited</i> I was. I mean, really. Plus, there was yet another book coming! Hey, don't judge me too harshly. It's not like I had GR to jump onto so I could see (Mediator #5)! And it certainly didn't show on the book's spine, I'll tell ya that much.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/8d5c79022eef2e1ecf6575c282c8c250_zpsmtdeffk8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Yeah," I said. "Yeah, this is my room now. So you're going to have to clear out."<br>"<i>I'm</i> going to have to clear out?" He raised one black eyebrow. "This has been my home for a century and a half. Why do <i>I</i> have to leave it?"</blockquote>
</b><br><br>But in some weird way....<b>I think that's why I loved this series so much</b>. It was developed and Jesse was in full-blown swoon mode and Suze was funnier than ever-and hey, there was lots of jelly at this point...me likes the jelly boys. So, you know, maybe my little heart needed this one first. *Shrugs* I dunno.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Just before I fell asleep again, I thought I heard something besides the owl. It sounded like someone singing the words <i>Oh, Susannah, now don't you cry for me, 'cause I come from Alabama with this banjo on my knee.</i><br>But that, I'm sure, was just my imagination. </blockquote>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_n1y00wnIfO1qdgslmo2_500_zps5gwofzz1.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Witty, light-hearted, fun, fast-paced, and humorous, I will never get tired of reading about Suze's escapades as a mediator. I mean really, who gets to have a sexy, mysterious ghost boy as a roommate? Certainly not I....but I sure would have loved to have had a Jesse of my own. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

</a><br><br><br>*****<br><br>Oh. My. GOD guys....that moment when you realize a childhood favorite is <u>better than anything you remember</u> and you get <i>three times</i> the feels because you can ACTUALLY UNDERSTAND IT BETTER and <b>appreciate your young childhood BBF</b> in the way he deserves AGHHHH.<br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_inline_mjxasqBtcg1qz4rgp_zpsyz0p7uqb.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br>Sometimes it feels like coming home when you pick up a book again...and that's all you can really ask for. Those feels, they are unlike anything you've ever felt. SO unreal. And so worth it to re read these masterpieces from my childhood.<br><br>RTC<br><br>***********<br><br>Ahhhh nostalgiaaaaaaaa ♥<br><br><br>**********<br><br><br>O.m.g. My favorite book series EVER from when I was in middle school is being made into a movie! You know how many times I wished that would happen 10 or more years ago?! I used to pick out songs that would make up the soundtrack. <br><br>I will be there! Hope they don't ruin it!</span>

<div id="review_10405018" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10405018" />
    <a title="Leanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/335117-leanna"><img alt="Leanna" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10405018?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leanna" href="/user/show/335117-leanna">Leanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10405018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2982731322389390056">I’ve developed a really bad habit: book cheating.<br/><br/>Until recently, I’ve had impeccable reading etiquette. I never flip to the end of the book. I don’t cheat to see if the lovers reconcile or to discover who the murderer is. Instead, I read from cover to cover. It’s only right.<br/><br/>But lately I’ve found myself cheating. I can’t help it—it’s those pesky young adult serials I’ve been reading. They simply aren’t good enough to justify reading the whole series, but they are interesting enough that I want to</span>
  <span id="freeText2982731322389390056" style="display:none">I’ve developed a really bad habit: book cheating.<br /><br />Until recently, I’ve had impeccable reading etiquette. I never flip to the end of the book. I don’t cheat to see if the lovers reconcile or to discover who the murderer is. Instead, I read from cover to cover. It’s only right.<br /><br />But lately I’ve found myself cheating. I can’t help it—it’s those pesky young adult serials I’ve been reading. They simply aren’t good enough to justify reading the whole series, but they are interesting enough that I want to know what happens. So I’ve started looking online to discover how the series end. I know, shameful.<br /><br />I never should have started three YA series in one week. Such an overdose could only be dangerous. The latest culprit: Meg Cabot’s The Mediator series. I just finished the first book, Shadowland, and I had to know what happened to the protagonist, Suze, so I cheated.<br /><br />Suze is a “mediator.” Basically, she is a teen Ghost Whisperer. I confess I have watched—and even enjoyed—the TV series, so I was a bit intrigued by the idea of a teenage girl who both sees ghosts and helps them “cross” to the other side.<br /><br />The premise is interesting, and the book is a fairly entertaining read. However, it is not entertaining enough to persuade me to read the other five books in the series.<br /><br />On the other hand, Suze happens to share her bedroom with a nineteenth-century-hottie-cowboy ghost. How could I not cheat to find out how the ghost and the teenage girl progress romantically?<br /><br />Clearly, the cure to my problem is no more young adult serials. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2982731322389390056" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2372317674?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=california">california</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2372317674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17699361519176756495">My first thought was that this would be some overdramatic teen novel that would quickly get buried under layers of drama and romance, but actually it was really complex, funny, imaginative and powerful as far as YA bestsellers go. I loved the main character, how she wasn't just some cookie-cutter girl and had her own unconventional style and personality. The Californian setting definitely added an atmosphere of summer sunshine and bright nostalgia to the book, and it was full of unexpected surpr</span>
  <span id="freeText17699361519176756495" style="display:none">My first thought was that this would be some overdramatic teen novel that would quickly get buried under layers of drama and romance, but actually it was really complex, funny, imaginative and powerful as far as YA bestsellers go. I loved the main character, how she wasn't just some cookie-cutter girl and had her own unconventional style and personality. The Californian setting definitely added an atmosphere of summer sunshine and bright nostalgia to the book, and it was full of unexpected surprises. I really loved <i>Shadowland</i> and I'd definitely recommend it to any reader.</span>

<div id="review_1518845313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1518845313" />
    <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner"><img alt="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588471351p2/7366569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1518845313?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1518845313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4469017828590027289"><a href='https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/2016/06/06/review-shadowland/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Review posted on Fafa's Book Corner </a>!<br/><br/>Beware spoilers ahead!<br/><br/>When I was younger I was a fan of Meg Cabot. As far as I was concerned she could do no wrong and that all her books were fantastic! Last year I discovered that it's not true. I found out that I didn't like her contemporary books. But I still immensely enjoyed her paranormal/supernatural books. This year I remembered this series and was happy to find that my library has it! I am happy to say that I enjoyed this!<br/><br/>The book begins with Suze </span>
  <span id="freeText4469017828590027289" style="display:none"><a href="https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/2016/06/06/review-shadowland/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Review posted on Fafa's Book Corner </a>!<br /><br />Beware spoilers ahead!<br /><br />When I was younger I was a fan of Meg Cabot. As far as I was concerned she could do no wrong and that all her books were fantastic! Last year I discovered that it's not true. I found out that I didn't like her contemporary books. But I still immensely enjoyed her paranormal/supernatural books. This year I remembered this series and was happy to find that my library has it! I am happy to say that I enjoyed this!<br /><br />The book begins with Suze mentioning the differences between New York and California. Her mother has gotten remarried and they had to shift to California because Andy her step dad owns a business there. Suze actually likes Andy and she doesn't mind Dopey, Sleepy, and Doc (her nicknames for her step brothers) but she doesn't like the fact that they had to move. Suze doesn't share these thoughts with her mother. Andy makes her mother very happy and Suze is okay with that.<br /><br />Her new family take her home. On the way there she notices again how different Cali is from New York. While they are talking it comes out that the school she'll be attending is a very old building. As is there house. After hearing this Suze starts to freak out because she doesn't like old buildings.<br /><br />When they get to the house Suze tries to remain calm. Andy has put a lot of work into the house and has tried to make it comfortable for her. Once they reach Suze's room she sees a guy sitting at her window seat. Only the rest of her family don't see him. Suze can see ghosts and usually there are more ghosts in old buildings.<br /><br />I seriously did not expect to enjoy Shadowland this much! It was so much fun! This book is written in first person told in Suze's point of view. It takes place over the course of a few days.<br /><br />I loved Suze. She is definitely my favourite Meg Cabot character! She was smart and a bit of a hot-head. She was tough and could handle a fight just fine.It was interesting to read about her experience with ghosts. And how the mediator stuff works. Throughout this book Suze trying to help people ends up being a bit reckless. She never accepts anyone's help she goes solo. Throughout the book she decides to work with other and that it isn't so bad.<br /><br />The relationships were awesome! I loved how close Suze was with her mother and that she didn't mind her step father. It's nice to read about a good step parent. While Suze isn't close to any of her brothers in the beginning of the book she does develop a good relationship with Doc. It was so sweet reading about! It wasn't always rainbows and sunshine but they were there for each other.<br /><br />The little I read about Cece and Adam was nice. I liked Father Dom and Jesse. Father Dom is the principle (and a priest) of the school that Suze attends. Much to her surprise he is also a mediator and does offer to train her. He was a nice mentor. Jesse was a bit clueless but sweet. This does take place in a few days so there isn't really any romance. Suze does consider Jesse good looking but at the moment they're just friends.<br /><br />The plot was pretty good. Heather was realistic. There are definitely girls like her. It was also nice to for a change that Suze didn't like her powers. But that didn't mean that she was rude to people she still did all her ghostly duty without a lot of complaints. I admire her for that.<br /><br />I only had two problems with Shadowland. There were times when Suze would talk about how good looking Jesse that it would become annoying. And while I understood why she did so there were times when I felt it wasn't necessary. Also I find it very weird that in a matter of a day Suze is very popular. Yes she did save one of the students and threaten to break another students fingers, I don't think it's possible to get popular that fast. Nonetheless I enjoyed this!<br /><br />Overall this was a really good book! I recommend this series to anyone looking for a completed fantasy that it more focused on the character development.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4469017828590027289" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_201343109" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/201343109" />
    <a title="Gergana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana"><img alt="Gergana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439319393p2/5312798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201343109?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gergana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gergana" href="/user/show/5312798-gergana">Gergana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312798-gergana?shelf=ya">ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201343109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13355022749240547957"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473867158i/20524891._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Fanarts and random images included! Yey! <br/><br/><i>Disclaimer: Rereading and reviewing some of my old-time favourites. First read in 2010, last reread in Summer, 2016</i><br/><br/>WARNING: <br/>1. This is a review for the first (6 books). The new book that was published earlier in 2016 will be reviewed separately.<br/>2. No spoilers are included.<br/>3. This series has many many many many flaws, avoid if you're not a fan of YA by all cost!<br/>4. My logic is purely emotional (as usual), you might want to check a few more reviews.<br/>5. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473867323i/20524926._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473867323i/20524927._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Ahhh, </span>
  <span id="freeText13355022749240547957" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473867158i/20524891._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fanarts and random images included! Yey! <br><br><i>Disclaimer: Rereading and reviewing some of my old-time favourites. First read in 2010, last reread in Summer, 2016</i><br><br>WARNING: <br>1. This is a review for the first (6 books). The new book that was published earlier in 2016 will be reviewed separately.<br>2. No spoilers are included.<br>3. This series has many many many many flaws, avoid if you're not a fan of YA by all cost!<br>4. My logic is purely emotional (as usual), you might want to check a few more reviews.<br>5. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473867323i/20524926._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473867323i/20524927._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Ahhh, 2010 - the year when people were still waging wars over who should hook up with Bella from Twilight, panicking over which vampire book they should read next, or wondering whether they should just move on something more serious (such as fallen angels). And there was one website that offered the solution to all our problems...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473885251i/20527412._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473885251i/20527413._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473885251i/20527414._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473885251i/20527415._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473885251i/20527416._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473885251i/20527417._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>############################<br><br><b>STORY</b><br><br>The books follow Suze, an extroverted and mischievous teenager about to start her new life in beautiful, sunny California, along with her mum, step dad and three step brothers. New house, new school and a new roommate...who happens to be dead. Yep, Jesse, a hot "young" cowboy with KILLER ABS (as we are kindly reminded a thousand times by our protagonist) politely refuses to vacate her bedroom, mainly because he doesn't know where else to go and he doesn't want to leave the only person who can actually see and communicate with him. As creepy as this sounds, Jesse is a very old-fashioned gentleman so he never really abuses Suze's privacy. Just go with it.<br><br>Suze is a Mediator, a person who can talk with ghosts and help them move to ...to... to whatever follows after death. If she's lucky, all our heroine needs to do is help the dead person complete their unfinished business and she's free to lead a normal life, worrying about boyfriends and school. Most of the cases, however, involve murder mysteries, vengeful ghosts and dangerous psychopaths.<br><br>############################<br><br><b> MY THOUGHTS</b><br><br><i>
  <b>PROS<b></b></b>
</i><br><br>Witty, fast-paced, humorous, filled with action, mysteries, ghosts and romance (of a sort), extreme cheesiness that makes me giggle, easy to follow writing style and descriptions that would make you feel like you're on a beach in California. These books are super innocent, non-pretentious, rather simple and, although I first read them in my early twenties, I found myself thoroughly enjoying them once more.<br><br>Yes, the plot isn't anything phenomenal, yet, it's interesting enough to finish all six books in less than two week(Plus, they're really short.)<br><br>Yes, the characters can be on-dimensional and predictable (with a few exceptions), but they still manage to be charming and entertaining. <br><br>The "romance" was...ok, I suppose. I couldn't really connect to Suze, but Jesse was cute :D <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I didn't even mind the Love triangle!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>
  <b>CONS<b></b></b>
</i><br><br>There are series that you can reread a hundred times and each time the experience will only get better and better.The Mediator series, unfortunately, wasn't one of those series. Don't get me wrong, there is a lot that makes these 6 books highly enjoyable, but I've become super fussy when it comes to YA books featuring horny teenage girls with special snowflake syndrome and complete lack of brains. (I blame age and too many awesome books). <br><br>It takes four books for Suze to start acting... "maturely", to stop relying on Jesse to save her, to stop drooling over his abs and to start taking this mediating business more seriously. 4 books can be a long time. In addition, she can be rather dislikable, easy to anger, mean and seriously <b>self-centred</b>...seriously...<br><br>The writing style can become rather annoying and repetitive. Especially since we're in Suze head all the time and she isn't the brightest person around.<br><br>Of course, we are all entitled to our own opinion.<br><br>############################<br><br><b>WILL I RECOMMEND TO FRIENDS </b><br><br>If you're looking for short, cosy read, to take your mind away from everyday life, if you don't want to read anything complicated and detailed at the moment, if you just want to have fun and a good laugh, feel free to give The Mediator series a go.<br><br>Me, personally, I doubt I'll be rereading these any time soon. Nevertheless...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473867994i/20524999._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>...Jesse's so cute!<br><br>############################<br><br>If you're looking for some good ghost books, check if these will be any good for you:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13555073.The_Screaming_Staircase__Lockwood___Co____1_" title="The Screaming Staircase (Lockwood &amp; Co., #1) by Jonathan Stroud" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1369670906s/13555073.jpg" alt="The Screaming Staircase (Lockwood &amp; Co., #1) by Jonathan Stroud" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> - One of my favourites! Set in an alternative world where Great Britain has been infested by ghosts and the only people who can fight them are children wielding rapiers, chains and all kinds of gadgets. First book is mildly scary, but by the third book I was absolutely terrified!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9378297.Anna_Dressed_in_Blood__Anna___1_" title="Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1398637405s/9378297.jpg" alt="Anna Dressed in Blood (Anna, #1) by Kendare Blake" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> - didn't finish this one (lost interest around second half), but from what I can remember, it was really dark and scary. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2800905.The_Summoning__Darkest_Powers___1_" title="The Summoning (Darkest Powers, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1327890699s/2800905.jpg" alt="The Summoning (Darkest Powers, #1) by Kelley Armstrong" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> - if you're looking for another YA series, this one might be worth checking out. Includes all kinds of paranormal creatures (werewolves, magicians etc.). Slight warning though - the pacing is really slow and the ending is a little bit...disappointing.<br> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9022772404916859484">I decided I wanted to reread this book series because it was one of my all-time favorites when I was in high school. I'm not sure if a new reader would enjoy it now, but I still loved it. It's pretty much classic teen chick lit, and a fun, breezy read. If you like spunky main characters that fight ghosts, you might like this.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_980745466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/980745466" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563502369p2/23218431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/980745466?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/23218431-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=cozy-cozy-cozy">cozy-cozy-cozy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=a-whole-lot-of-fun">a-whole-lot-of-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=best-of-2018">best-of-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=the-fluff">the-fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=likable-heroines">likable-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=kickass-heroines">kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23218431-sharon?shelf=romance">romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer980745466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer615847583217172418">I have been dyingggg to read this (pardon my pun LOL) ever since I finished Cabot’s <i>Heather Wells</i> series. She once again manages to write such a fun, well-rounded series!<br/><br/>Here are some of my thoughts:<br/>•	The protagonist, Suze, is confident and not afraid to speak her mind and talk back to bullies. I love that. It is so funny to see her interact with other people. Usually I would think the “new kid in school” would feel shy, but on the very first day, she stood her ground and was just herself. So pr</span>
  <span id="freeText615847583217172418" style="display:none">I have been dyingggg to read this (pardon my pun LOL) ever since I finished Cabot’s <i>Heather Wells</i> series. She once again manages to write such a fun, well-rounded series!<br /><br />Here are some of my thoughts:<br />•	The protagonist, Suze, is confident and not afraid to speak her mind and talk back to bullies. I love that. It is so funny to see her interact with other people. Usually I would think the “new kid in school” would feel shy, but on the very first day, she stood her ground and was just herself. So props to that. Also, I appreciate that she is family-oriented. Some of my favorite scenes are just seeing her interact and grow closer to her new stepfather (who is so kind) &amp; stepbrothers. And even though she was sulking in the beginning about changing school and being in a whole new state, you can tell how she genuinely wants her mom to be happy and that overpowers anything else. Really strong family theme, which I adore.<br />•	In particular, her twelve-year-old brother, Dave, is such a sweetie. I am glad to see Suze warm up to him. It is cute how he wants to make her happy and comfortable. <br />•	Besides the family theme, there is also a friendship theme (although not as strong as the family theme). Suze is really respectful and nice with them. I am glad this is not one of those silly, cliché stories where the new girl struggles between choosing friends who accept her but are considered “freaks” and the popular crowd. There is no struggle here. She did not once consider dumping her friends just because she got the attention of the popular crowd. She was just like “Oh. You guys didn’t get invited to her party? That’s cool, I’m not going anymore because who else am I going to talk to?” Props to not having unnecessary drama and finally seeing a level-headed, down-to-earth protagonist. Good role model.<br />•	I can’t wait to see how her relationship will change with the other 2 stepbrothers who she is not close as close with. <br />•	I like Jesse. The way he banters with Suze and they have a love-hate thing going on is cute. Curious to see how her relationship will evolve with him as well. <br />•	Her camaraderie with the priest is so funny and cute. I am glad that she has someone to talk to about being a mediator.<br />•	I appreciate that this book is primarily about Suze seeing her new home and school, and learning to accept her new life here. She adjusted to it quite swimmingly.<br /><br />Overall, it is just a really fun storyline with a truly likable heroine. Because this is a pretty long series, I can’t wait to dive in and become more addicted (hopefully).<br /><br /><u>Things that you might want to know <b>(WARNING: Spoilers below)</b></u><br />Happy/satisfying ending? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes, peaceful ending, but not the last book as storyline is still continuing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Love triangle? Cheating? Angst level? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There is somewhat of a love triangle, but it is very low-key. It is so anti-drama, and I love it. This book I about Suze meeting new characters, and she has interest in one guy she met at school which is very light-hearted and quite cute. And then, there’s another guy she is learning about and getting interested in, which is a ghost. No drama whatsoever in this area, and idk it was just fun to read. This book has romance but it is flowing casually so far.<br /><br />No cheating. Low angst. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Tears-worthy? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Humor? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Favorite scenes? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I don’t know, I simply enjoyed this from beginning to end. I really did enjoy her getting closer to her stepbrother, Dave. When Dave and Sleepy (forgot his real name) go to save Suze. When her stepdad checks in on her after they gave her a sick day, and he makes her a sandwich and just chat with her one-on-one. And I love the Jesse scenes. And when she talked back towards the mean girls during class time without sweating it. When she and the priest are checking in on each other. Also, the scene where she goes to the beach with her friends, and the sun is setting and she feels at peace for the first time, and she and her friends at start singing Here Comes the Sun together. Aw. That was a really well-done scene. And at the end when her mother is checking up on her and she realizes how truly happy her mom looks ever since moving here and she is happy for her, and they watch the sunset together. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />What age level would be appropriate? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Vague mentions of sex. Some cussing. One character shows to be homophobic, but it is obviously shown as wrong and he is reprimanded. Pre-teens/teens and up. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="615847583217172418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172320060" />
    <a title="Amy (Turn the Page)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5535721-amy-turn-the-page"><img alt="Amy (Turn the Page)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343817781p2/5535721.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172320060?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy (Turn the Page)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy (Turn the Page)" href="/user/show/5535721-amy-turn-the-page">Amy (Turn the Page)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5535721-amy-turn-the-page?shelf=old-favourite">old-favourite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172320060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18204433112430741806">Firstly, let me just say, I doubt you’ll ever read a bad review of a Meg Cabot book from me. I love the woman (her blog is hilarious). In fact, I have a whole (rather pink) bookshelf dedicated to all of her books that I own, which, I’ll admit now, is pretty much most of them. If I’m looking for a great, fun, story, likeable heroines (and a tension filled romance with a ridiculously attractive guy), Meg Cabot never lets me down. I’ll buy her newest book as soon as it comes out, without waiting fo</span>
  <span id="freeText18204433112430741806" style="display:none">Firstly, let me just say, I doubt you’ll ever read a bad review of a Meg Cabot book from me. I love the woman (her blog is hilarious). In fact, I have a whole (rather pink) bookshelf dedicated to all of her books that I own, which, I’ll admit now, is pretty much most of them. If I’m looking for a great, fun, story, likeable heroines (and a tension filled romance with a ridiculously attractive guy), Meg Cabot never lets me down. I’ll buy her newest book as soon as it comes out, without waiting for the paperback and devour it the same day.<br /><br />The Mediator series is one of my favourites. I read them all in less than a week over the Easter break way back when. Sadly, nowadays, my well-loved copies are starting to fall apart. I do intend to eventually review each book in the series, six in total for you guys, but for now, here’s my review on the first book, Shadowland.<br /><br />Meg Cabot’s heroines are always a perfect blend of sharp wit, humour, fiery independence, and quirkiness. (They are also usually just slightly insane which you can't help but love). Your everyday girl, that any teenager (or adult *ahem*) reader can easily relate to. This book is no exception. Susannah Simon, or ‘Suzie’, is instantly likeable, sarcastic with a tough demeanour and fiercely protective of her friends and family. And she kicks ghost butt. What’s not to like?<br /><br />The plotline here is pretty basic (the blurb above just about covers it), but engaging nevertheless. Cabot draws you in with just enough action, a loveable heroine, one very attractive dead cowboy, and endearing secondary characters to keep you interested. In true style, Cabot ends with a mystery or two (and the promise of a sizzling romantic plot line), to leave you coming back for more. I dare you to try and put it down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18204433112430741806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1281992790563530252">I forgot how much I absolutely loved these books. I mean <i> LOVE </i> these books. There's just something about them that makes me ridiculously happy each time I read them, and they really never get old. <br/><br/>Cabot has a way with her writing that makes her books extremely easy to read, without them being boring or childish and I think that's a feat in itself.   <span id="freeText1281992790563530252" style="display:none">I forgot how much I absolutely loved these books. I mean <i> LOVE </i> these books. There's just something about them that makes me ridiculously happy each time I read them, and they really never get old. <br /><br />Cabot has a way with her writing that makes her books extremely easy to read, without them being boring or childish and I think that's a feat in itself. Then there's the characters she's created. Everyone from Suze to Doc, Grumpy, and Sleepy, to Ceecee and Adam and of course, Jesse, really comes to life just in this first book and you can't help but love them all in their own way. <br /><br />Yes, the book is full of your usual high-school novel stereotypes, but they aren't shoved in your face so much that you get annoyed, they're just floating around in the background for the most part. <br /><br />All I know is, I absolutely cannot wait to continue reading this series... again. But mostly so I can get to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27412183.Proposal__The_Mediator___6_5_" title="Proposal (The Mediator, #6.5) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Proposal</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25573701.Remembrance__The_Mediator___7_" title="Remembrance (The Mediator, #7) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Remembrance</a> ;p <br /><br /><br />**First (documented) Read- April 2012<br />***First Re-read- February 2016</span>

<div id="review_1206257424" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206257424" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1206257424?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=paranormal-urban-fantasy">paranormal-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1206257424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15107546295251817571">Meg Cabot can tell a story. This is the second time I'm reading this series (first time reading around 4 years ago), not remembering almost anything from it, and I really liked it. <br/><br/>It has got pretty streightforward plot, captivating enough without being overwhelming, as it's only a first book in a series. <br/><br/>The MC has a strong and interesting voice. There's also a great cast of secondary characters. One of them being Doc (Suze's know-it-all younger half brother), Father Dominic (the principal) and</span>
  <span id="freeText15107546295251817571" style="display:none">Meg Cabot can tell a story. This is the second time I'm reading this series (first time reading around 4 years ago), not remembering almost anything from it, and I really liked it. <br /><br />It has got pretty streightforward plot, captivating enough without being overwhelming, as it's only a first book in a series. <br /><br />The MC has a strong and interesting voice. There's also a great cast of secondary characters. One of them being Doc (Suze's know-it-all younger half brother), Father Dominic (the principal) and of course Jesse (the love interest). <br /><br />There's very light hint on the future romance that has yet to happen, and I really liked the fact that there was almost none in this first book. The romance takes time to start. Sure, Suze does appreciate the view, but we have to wait for the romantic feelings to develop. I also liked the writing, we really got to know Suze's voice and personality through it. <br /><br />This is one of those books I wish I've read when I started with YA fantasy genre (around the age of 13). I would've absolutely loved and adored it then. I can still enjoy and appreciate this series now though.<br /><br /><br />My rating of The Mediator series - <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/187811.Shadowland__The_Mediator___1_" title="Shadowland (The Mediator, #1) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadowland</a> ★★★☆☆ (3.5/5 stars)<br /><br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/199786.Ninth_Key__The_Mediator___2_" title="Ninth Key (The Mediator, #2) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Ninth Key</a> ★★★☆☆ (3.5/5 stars)<br /><br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/199785.Reunion__The_Mediator___3_" title="Reunion (The Mediator, #3) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Reunion</a> ★★★☆☆ (2.5 ish/5 stars)<br /><br />4. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23224.Darkest_Hour__The_Mediator___4_" title="Darkest Hour (The Mediator, #4) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkest Hour</a> ★★★☆☆ (3.5/5 stars)<br /><br />5. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23225.Haunted__The_Mediator___5_" title="Haunted (The Mediator, #5) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Haunted</a> ★★★☆☆ (2.75/5 stars)<br /><br />6. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/93724.Twilight__The_Mediator___6_" title="Twilight (The Mediator, #6) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a> ★★★☆☆ (3/5 stars)<br /><br />Additional :<br /><br />7. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25573701.Remembrance__The_Mediator___7_" title="Remembrance (The Mediator, #7) by Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Remembrance</a> ☆☆☆☆☆ (DNF at the beginning, pretending it does not exist)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15107546295251817571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=paranormal-general">paranormal-general</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161373622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11810600562148883846">I resisted Meg Cabot for so long...but turns out she's pretty fun. This first book in The Mediator series surprised me with its fast-paced story, humor, and entertaining characters. The plotting of the mystery is not particularly complicated, but that's something I expected from seeing the cover art and reading the blurbs. It's pretty much chick lit for teens with a dose of the supernatural to sweeten in it up.<br/><br/>What did bother me, though, was that the author used the word "fag" twice in this book</span>
  <span id="freeText11810600562148883846" style="display:none">I resisted Meg Cabot for so long...but turns out she's pretty fun. This first book in The Mediator series surprised me with its fast-paced story, humor, and entertaining characters. The plotting of the mystery is not particularly complicated, but that's something I expected from seeing the cover art and reading the blurbs. It's pretty much chick lit for teens with a dose of the supernatural to sweeten in it up.<br /><br />What did bother me, though, was that the author used the word "fag" twice in this book, and then the word shows up again on page 8 of the second book. Now, the person who used it was grounded for it, but I was surprised to see how casually the whole thing was handled. I'm not sure if the author was trying to make a point or not, but it does seem weird that it kept popping up again and again, and pretty much out of the blue. Doesn't add anything to the story and it's an odd detail. I googled to see if there were any discussions on this topic in relation to Meg Cabot's books, but couldn't find anything...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11810600562148883846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer328270974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5242136845424072227">Each of the six books in this series is fairly short, which might put some people off spending money on them. Luckily these were a library find, so I didn't have to decide if it was worth it to me. I probably would have missed out otherwise, because I ended up loving them.<br/><br/>The series is light and humorous while dealing with some serious stuff (death, ghosts, murder, passage to the other side). I really love the setting in a small town in California. There's a feeling of history to it - of the day</span>
  <span id="freeText5242136845424072227" style="display:none">Each of the six books in this series is fairly short, which might put some people off spending money on them. Luckily these were a library find, so I didn't have to decide if it was worth it to me. I probably would have missed out otherwise, because I ended up loving them.<br /><br />The series is light and humorous while dealing with some serious stuff (death, ghosts, murder, passage to the other side). I really love the setting in a small town in California. There's a feeling of history to it - of the days of Spanish influence. This adds a completely different flavor than you get in most urban fantasies or paranormals that I've read. If you're thinking 'pink princessy diary' thoughts about Meg Cabot, don't. This might as well be a different author, aside from the light, witty tone.<br /><br />It's been a couple of years since I read them, but it's one of those series that will just pop into my mind occasionally. Not anything specific about the plot - it's more like catching a scent that reminds me of a feeling. I imagine I'll read them again one day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5242136845424072227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/689250815" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14826005-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406503164p2/14826005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/689250815?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/14826005-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Unknown Binding 9780743430500" href="/book/show/290013.Shadowland">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689250815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17577007524488611918">This is the same plot used for every other story about people who channel ghosts, except less compassionate, with more emphasis on being shallow, and it doesn't give a rat's ass about telling the story of the deceased.<br/><br/>The world building... Well, there's a beach and it's peaceful and there's religion and stuff. I guess since this is the real world, we don't need too much, but what we were given was just sort of... There.<br/><br/>Our main character is Susannah Simon. She's a previous outcast who, having ap</span>
  <span id="freeText17577007524488611918" style="display:none">This is the same plot used for every other story about people who channel ghosts, except less compassionate, with more emphasis on being shallow, and it doesn't give a rat's ass about telling the story of the deceased.<br /><br />The world building... Well, there's a beach and it's peaceful and there's religion and stuff. I guess since this is the real world, we don't need too much, but what we were given was just sort of... There.<br /><br />Our main character is Susannah Simon. She's a previous outcast who, having appeared as the new girl in a school, is suddenly loved by everyone. She threatens her classmates, is rude to the teachers, and switches between feeling "sympathetic" with our dead girl and not giving a damn about her worries. Also, she's shallower than a raindrop.<br />I really feel that Meg Cabot has only one protagonist, whose name she changes and slips into everything.<br />Other character can be split safely into two groups: Evil girls who tan and care about fashion, and friendly people who do not but are still judged for poor clothing coordination. When men tan and/or dress well, they're received positively and complimented on it. And there's a priest who's good-natured but incompetent.<br />On another note, who gets "Jesse" from <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hector de Silva <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>?<br /><br />This book needs editing.<br />Our narrator switches between topics and rambles for pages, distracting us from getting complete stories or even caring what mundane detail they wish to describe to us. They also think we forget cliche details like the romance-obsessed mother and outcast status of Susannah.<br /><br />In short, this is an uninspiring book with shallow characters and shallow effort.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17577007524488611918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1370276650" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1370276650" />
    <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj"><img alt="Nasty Lady MJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506395877p2/4026143.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1370276650?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasty Lady MJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasty Lady MJ" href="/user/show/4026143-nasty-lady-mj">Nasty Lady MJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=it-s-vintage">it-s-vintage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4026143-nasty-lady-mj?shelf=binge-read-material">binge-read-material</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1370276650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12110660094055918556">Really 3.5 stars. Solid but not my favorite in the series. I think my original review holds up well, just adjusting the rating since I think upon reread its closer to a three than four star read. <br/><br/>To see review with spiffy gif click <a href='https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/08/23/the-great-mediator-reread-shadowland-by-meg-cabot/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here.</a><br/><br/>A few months ago I reread all of the Princess Diaries series in anticipation of the adult installment that was released back in June. I decided to do the same thing with The Mediator series-which I actually prefer to Diaries. The seventh book will be released in </span>
  <span id="freeText12110660094055918556" style="display:none">Really 3.5 stars. Solid but not my favorite in the series. I think my original review holds up well, just adjusting the rating since I think upon reread its closer to a three than four star read. <br /><br />To see review with spiffy gif click <a href="https://howdyyal.wordpress.com/2015/08/23/the-great-mediator-reread-shadowland-by-meg-cabot/" rel="nofollow noopener">here.</a><br /><br />A few months ago I reread all of the Princess Diaries series in anticipation of the adult installment that was released back in June. I decided to do the same thing with The Mediator series-which I actually prefer to Diaries. The seventh book will be released in February 2016. Between now and then, I’ll be reading one book of the series a month (well, reviewing, there will probably be a point in time where I’ll binge read the rest of the series because that’s just how I do things).<br /><br />Original Reading Experience: <br /><br />I actually first read this book after I read the fifth one. Long story short, the publication of this series was a little weird. So I only started picking them up after they were published under Meg Cabot’s name, and I thought Haunted was a standalone. I am glad to say it’s not though-a stand alone. However, when you first read this book after the fifth one things can feel a little disjointed.<br /><br />Reread: <br /><br />It was enjoyable. I’ll admit that this book did feel a bit watered down to some YA books I’ve read. The prose seemed relatively simple to what I’ve been reading lately. And it’s short, not even three hundred pages. But it still worked.<br /><br />As far as Meg Cabot books go, this one wasn’t terribly dated. Often when I reread her stuff-especially The Princess Diaries series-I cringe when I read some of the outdated pop culture references. Shadowland had a few, but not near as many as other books.<br /><br />Some of the jokes are way stale though. And I really find Brad, the homophobe, offensive. Grant it, at the time of publication his offensiveness was more common than it is now. And at least Suze tells him off for it, but still Dopey is an ass.<br /><br />Suze is still fantastic as she was all those years ago. I still want her life. Her boots. And most importantly Jesse. I really enjoy how the romance isn’t in your face in the first installment. It’s amusing how Suze is not head over heals in love with him.<br /><br />Or the fact that Jesse doesn’t overwhelm the plot. That in itself is refreshing. And I love how Cabot just depicts him altogether. A lot of the time out of time heros come off as being a little stiff at best (at worst borderline offensive), but Jesse just works.<br /><br />But what I found to be the most interesting thing upon reread is how short books can work. Too often in today’s YA world we’re dealt with omnibus tomes that can just go on and on forever. Doing something short and concise is no easy feat and Cabot does it.<br /><br />As for the ghost: Oh, Heather. As far as ghosts go she’s one of least memorable ghosts in this series, but she does set a nice introduction to the art of mediation. She is a bit of a cliche though. But I can deal with that since it’s the first book.<br /><br />Overall, a nice reread and fairly strong start to my favorite YA series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12110660094055918556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1485096534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1485096534" />
    <a title="Aoife" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife"><img alt="Aoife" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514771423p2/16768476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1485096534?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoife" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoife" href="/user/show/16768476-aoife">Aoife</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6571575-shadowland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=favourite-author">favourite-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16768476-aoife?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1485096534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3174665081372087391">I first read this series when I was between 14-16 years old I believe and I really loved it so when I found out a new novel was coming in February 2016 with a grow-up Suze, I knew I had to reread the series.<br/><br/>I really loved going into this with a fresh pair of eyes and the knowledge I had the whole series to my disposal on my Kindle and wouldn't have to wait for the next one to show up on the library shelf (this was before the days of reserving books online, it was a 'you see it, you take it' kind</span>
  <span id="freeText3174665081372087391" style="display:none">I first read this series when I was between 14-16 years old I believe and I really loved it so when I found out a new novel was coming in February 2016 with a grow-up Suze, I knew I had to reread the series.<br /><br />I really loved going into this with a fresh pair of eyes and the knowledge I had the whole series to my disposal on my Kindle and wouldn't have to wait for the next one to show up on the library shelf (this was before the days of reserving books online, it was a 'you see it, you take it' kind of thing cause you didn't know when you'd see it again). I had forgotten alot of the series except for the basics - 16-year-old moves to California, she can see ghosts, hot ghost in bedroom, whole load of trouble.<br /><br />Suze is a great character, She's independent, spunky and confident but also has a degree of warmth and caring. She doesn't let bullies or snobs get away with anything and likes to share her opinions. One of the best things I loved about the book was Suze's family dynamic. I forgot how great it was. Despite the fact she hardly knew her stepbrothers, I always felt they settled down with one another really well and with a lovely level of caring, from David/Doc's fawning over Suze to Jake/Sleepy's role of big brother caring for little sister. There was very little angst between them other than some normal sibling squabbles and her relationship with her stepdad Andy was also lovely. The family life was healthy and great to read.<br /><br />I'm knocking off a half a star to the book basically because at times I felt uncomfortable with the attitude towards suicide. Suze's first ghost in the book, besides Jesse, killed herself after her boyfriend broke up with her and she became a malevolent spirit, intent on harm.I literally winced at how unfeeling Suze was at times and I'm not sure if the casual way she says "blow your head off" would go down as well in a book written today when society in general has a much better attitude towards mental health and suicide. There was basically nothing done to discover other reasons why Heather felt the need to shoot herself other than her relationship status and it definitely left the impression that she was just a stupid, shallow girl. There was also the use of the words "fag" and "fag hag" at one point which, again, I didn't enjoy at all. Though in fairness, Dopey did get a slap and grounded for saying it.<br /><br />Overall, I loved revisiting this book and I can't wait to read the rest. I've already fallen in love with Jesse. I hate the new covers though. I much prefer the old ones.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3174665081372087391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
